Jamison Brereton

24 (465)
Indra
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn begins, like the last one, with a strong statement of IndraтАЩs relationship with soma, but it then turns to more general praises of the god (vss. 2тАУ8), with some strik ing similes, metaphors, and etymological figures. The importance of mortal praise and worship for maintaining IndraтАЩs powers is not forgotten; see verses 7тАУ8 and especially verse 6, which seems to concern the traffic in praise: inspiration going out from Indra to the poets and then returning to him as praise (for a similar sentiment and phraseol ogy, see VI.34.1). The last two verses (9тАУ10) ask for IndraтАЩs gifts and protection.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAt the rites at which soma (is offered) the exhilaration (produced) in Indra is a shower (of benefits to the offerer); so is the chanted hymn with the (recited) prayer, therefore the drinker of the soma, the partaker of the stale soma, Maghavan, is to be propitiated by men with praises; dweller in heaven, he is the lord of sacred songs, unwearied in the protection (of his votaries).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bullish exuberance, noise, and solemn words are in Indra; he is the drinker of the pressings and in possession of the silvery drink, when the soma juices are in his company.
He is worthy to be chanted by men with solemn words as the bounteous one, the heaven-ruling king of hymns, whose help is imperishable.

Jamison Brereton Notes

That av─лс╕е of c is also the verb of d is suggested by passages like I.110.9 v─Б╠Бjebhir no v─Б╠Бjas─Бtau aviс╕Нс╕Нhi, VIII.46.11 dh├нyo v─Б╠Бjebhir ─Бvitha with тИЪav and an instr.

of v─Б╠Бja- тАШprizeтАЩ.

Griffith

STRONG rapturous joy, praise, glory are with Indra: impetuous God, he quaffs the juice of Soma:
That Maghavan whom men must laud with singing, Heaven-dweller, King of songs, whose help is lasting.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe surpasser (of foes), a hero, the friend of man, the discriminator, the hearer of the invocation, the great protector of his adorers, the giver of dwelings, the ruler of men, the cherisher of his worshippers, the bestower of food, grants us, when glorified at the sacrifice, (abundant) sustenance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The surpassing hero, favorable to men, discriminating, the hearer of the singerтАЩs call, whose help is wide-ranging,
the good one, the Laud of Men, who gives succor to bards, praised as the prizewinner, he gives the prize at the rite of distribution.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner supplies the verb тАШdriveтАЩ in c (тАЬMit diesen (treib) alle Angriffe auseinanderтАЭ), but I see no reason why it canтАЩt be in the orbit of d. In vs. 1 the two p─Бdas cd share a single verb (av─лс╕е c), as do the first two p─Бdas of this vs. (vyathay─Б).

With this pattern established, it seems reasonable to take ├бva t─Бr─лс╕е in d as also governing the accusatives of c. Under this interpr., I take v├нс╣г┼лc─лс╕е as proleptic, rather like 3d kс╣Ыс╣Зuh─л╠Бp├бr─Бcaс╕е тАЬput them far away.тАЭ

Griffith

He, Friend of man, most wise, victorious Hero, hears, with far-reaching aid, the singer call him.
Excellent, Praise of Men, the bard’s Supporter, Strong, he gives strength, extolled in holy synod.

Geldner

├Ьberwinder, Held, mannhaft, klug, Erh├╢rer des Rufes des S├дngers, weiten Schutz gew├дhrend, gut, der Preis der M├дnner, den Dichter ern├дhrend, als Sieger in der Opferrede gepriesen verleiht er den Siegerpreis.

Der Siegesheld, der tapfre und der weise, vernimmt den Ruf des S├дngers weitbeschirmend, Der M├дnner Lob, der gute, Dichter pflegend; gelobt beim Opfer gibt der reiche Reichthum.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMighty hero, by your magnitude, (the exten) of heaven and earth is exceeded, as the axle by the (circumerfence of the) wheels; invoked of many, your numerous benefits, Indra, spread out like the branches of a tree.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like an axle beyond its two wheels, your lofty (greatness), o champion, projects beyond the two worlds in their greatness. (Like) the branches of a tree, your forms of help have grown outward, o much-invoked Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c lacks a verb to govern the acc. vithur─Б╠Б┼Ы├бv─Бс╣Гsi. On the model of 1cd, 2ab, and 2cd, we might simply deploy the (first) verb of d, jah├н, across the p─Бda boundary: тАЬsmash their faltering powersтАЭ or, with proleptic adj., тАЬsmash their powers (to be) faltering.тАЭ However, vithur─Б╠Бis derived from the root тИЪvyath тАШfalterтАЩ, whose causative supplied the verb in 2ab, vyathay─Б. I therefore think thereтАЩs a different kind of trick here: the poet expects us to supply the CAUSATIVE feature of the verb in 2b with the lexical feature of that verb contained in the adj. vithur─Б╠Б– hence my tr.

тАЬ(render) their powers faltering.тАЭ

Griffith

The lofty axle of thy wheels, O Hero, is not surpassed by heaven and earth in greatness.
Like branches of a tree, Invoked of many manifold aids spring forth from thee, O Indra.

Geldner

Wie die Achse ├╝ber die beiden, so ragt, o Held, deine hohe Gr├╢├Яe an Umfang ├╝ber beide Welten hinaus. Wie die Zweige des Baumes so wachsen nach allen Seiten deine Gnaden, vielgerufener Indra.

Grassmann

Wie beide R├дder ├╝berragt die Achse, so beide Welten, deine Gr├╢ss’, o starker; O vielgerufner wie des Baumes Zweige entspriessen, Indra, deine vielen H├╝lfen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAccomplisher of many acts, the energies of you who are (ever) active (congregate from all directions), like the converging tracks of cattle; they are the bonds (of foes), themselves unfettered, munificent Indra, like the tethers of (many) calves.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The energies: ┼Ы─Бk─Бс╕е ┼Ыaktayaс╕е, abilities, energies; the verb is added: sarvataс╕е saс╣Гcarant─л, come together from all sides; gav─Бm iva srutayaс╕е sa├▒caraс╣З─лс╕е = dhen┼лn─Бm m─Бrg─Бс╕е yath─Б sarvatra sa├▒c─Бriс╣Зo bhavanti, as the paths of milch kine are everywhere going together; the translation is: vats─Бn─Бm na tantayaс╕е, like long ropes used to tie a number of calves together, like the tethers of many calves

Jamison Brereton

The abilities that belong to you, the able one, o you of many abilities, are converging like streams of cattle.
(They are) like cords for calves, Indra, binding without bonds, o you of good bonds [/gifts].

Jamison Brereton Notes

tan┼лr├║c- is, of course, a root noun cmpd., тАШshining with/in their bodiesтАЩ, but the bahuvr─лhi-like tr. works better in context.

kс╣Ыс╣Зva├нte is clearly meant as a 3rd du. mid. subjunctive to the 5th cl. pres. of тИЪkс╣Ы, but it has the wrong grade of the suffix: we expect *kс╣Ыn├бvaite (cf. 2nd du. mid.

a┼Ыn├бvaithe [VII.70.4]). It clearly simply anticipates the root pres. 3rd du. mid.

br├бvaite, which ends the next hemistich (4d). This imitation comes at a metrical cost: the heavy root syllable kс╣Ыс╣Зv produces a bad Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence. (The grammatically correct form would also, of course, be metrically problematic.) A root aor. subj.

*karaite would fit the meter better, but thereтАЩs no warrant for emendation. For a passage in which the poet simply avoids the middle dual subjunctive of тИЪkс╣Ы altogether by substituting a plural, see comm. ad I.178.2.

The locative string in cd is the usual expression of the stakes – a type of loc. absol. lacking an overt participle. The full expression is dh├бne hit├й тАЬwhen the stake is setтАЭ (VI.45.11, 13, etc.). The string here contains a formulaic pair, tok├й тАж t├бnaye тАЬprogeny and prosperityтАЭ with three other locc., one inserted inside the formula. On the basis of VI.31.1 (q.v.), where a ca after t├бnaye better delineates the pairing, I would slightly change the tr. to тАЬwhen progeny and prosperity [or, offspring and lineage], cattle, water, and fields are at stake.тАЭ The two v─Б-s (4a, 4c), in conjunction with the subjunctives, seem to set out a deliberative choice: тАЬit may be that X тАж or it may be that Y.тАЭ The two possibilities floated as to how one champion might defeat another set the stage for the next vs. (5), which forecloses any possibility that one of the champions, even a successful one, could take on Indra. The two v─Б-s are slightly off-balance, however, since the first one is located in the main clause (a) to which the first y├бd clause is immediately appended (b), while the second is found in the second y├бd clause, whose main clause seems to be, by default, the original p─Бda a. This seems to me a minor problem: the point is that the two champions (┼Ы┼л╠Бra-) in p─Бda a may defeat each other in single combat (b) or in a full-on battle (cd). The first v─Б would be better positioned in p─Бda b, but it has been shifted to the front of the whole main-cl./dep.-cl. construction – a sort of super-WackernagelтАЩs Law position. Klein (DGRV II.194, 201-2) treats the two v─Б occurrences separately, taking the 2nd as conjoining (or disjoining) the parallel y├бd clauses b and c, but the 1st as the equivalent of тАЬthe asseverative particle va├н.тАЭ This seems somewhat perverse to me: two occurrences of the same particle in a single verse, esp. a particle that regularly appears in pairs, invite a unified explanation; moreover, I am very dubious that v─Б is ever used for va├н, a particle that is rare in the RV anyway. Even Klein can only identify 6 passages where he thinks v─Б = va├н (DGRV II.201), of which he finds syntactic support for only 3. That 6c contains a pair of v─Б-s whose syntactic connection is clearer provides evidence that these two v─Б-s also form a pair.

Griffith

Strong Lord, thine energies, endowed with vigour, are like the paths of kine converging homeward.
Like bonds of cord, Indra, that bind the younglings, no bonds are they, O thou of boundless bounty.

English translation:

тАЬIndra achieves one act today, another tomorrow, evil and good repeatedly; may he, and Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, P┼лс╣гan, Arya, be on this occasion promoters of the desired result.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

One deed today and another tomorrow, one which is not and another which isтАФIndra makes (them) happen in an instant.
Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, also P┼лс╣гan, are there for us, but it is he [=Indra] who keeps the will of the stranger contained.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation of this vs. differs in a number of respects from the standard interpr. In particular, in the first hemistich, flg. an interpr. of JPBтАЩs, the two pairs any├бd ady├б k├бrvaraс╣Г any├бd u sv├бс╕е тАЬone deed today and another tomorrowтАЭ and ├бsac ca s├бt тАЬnon-existent and existentтАЭ are taken as a chiastic square, with any├бd ady├б matching s├бt and any├бd u sv├бс╕е matching ├бsat. In other words the deed Indra does today is existent, while the one he will do tomorrow is (as yet) non-existent. The standard interpr. takes ├бsat ca s├бt as an expression of process: Indra makes each deed (the one today, the one tomorrow) that was as yet non-existent into an existent one (so Geldner тАЬ… macht Indra das Unwirkliche alsbald wirklichтАЭ). This does seem a possible interpr., and I would suggest an alternative tr. тАЬOne deed today and another tomorrow – Indra makes the not (yet) existent (deed) existent.тАЭ Klein (DGRV I.170, II.24) takes ├бsac ca s├бt as тАЬthe bad and the good,тАЭ which deviates from the usual sense esp. of the former and breaks the thematic connection with the first p─Бda: тАЬ(Performing) one deed today and another tomorrow, Indra turns hither immediately the bad and the good.тАЭ In the 2nd hemistich the standard interpr. takes Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and P┼лс╣гan as the individualized seriatim singular subjects of paryet─Б╠Бsti (=paryet─Б╠Бasti), as in GeldnerтАЩs тАЬMitra und Varuс╣Зa und P┼лс╣гan kommen uns dabei dem Wunsche des Nebenbuhlers zuvor.тАЭ (Tichy [-tar-stems, 188] follows GeldnerтАЩs syntactic template, but with an aberrant interpr. of p├бri тИЪi.) As GeldnerтАЩs blithe disregard of the sg. verb shows, the triple subject is somewhat awkward given sg. asti (though singular verbs with a series of singular subjects are indeed found). But there are several other problematic aspects to this strain of interpr. On the syntactic level, it is surprising to find asti in a main clause if its function is simply copular (тАЬM, V, and P is/are pariet─Б╠БтАЭ); asti in main clauses is almost always existential. On the thematic level, these other gods are intrusive in the hymn – the focus so far has been entirely on Indra – and it seems odd suddenly to credit these gods with the power to effect a desirable thing for us, when Indra has been performing the heavy lifting all along. I therefore think that Thieme (Fremdling, 53) is correct in taking Indra as the unexpressed subject of pariet─Б╠Бasti, though he doesnтАЩt discuss the passage or, rather disingenuously, even quote the preceding p─Бda with the other possible subjects. Given these factors, I think that asti is implicitly contrastive and emphatic: the other gods are there for us in some sense, but itтАЩs Indra who тАж As for the sense of paryet─Б╠Бand p├бri тИЪi in general, the literal meaning is тАШgo aroundтАЩ, hence тАШencompassтАЩ and hence to contain and control, a sense that works very well here.

Griffith

One act to-day, another act tomorrow oft Indra makes what is not yet existent.
Here have we Mitra, Varuna, and Pusan to overcome the foeman’s domination.

Geldner

Heute ein anderes Werk und morgen ein anderes, macht Indra das Unwirkliche alsbald wirklich. Mitra und Varuna und Pusan kommen uns dabei dem Wunsche des Nebenbuhlers zuvor.

Grassmann

Ein andres wirkt er heute, andres morgen, was nicht ist, bringt zum Dasein pl├╢tzlich Indra, Wie Mitra hier, wie Varuna und Puschan ist er es, der des Feindes Macht bew├дltigt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy praises and by sacrifices, Indra, (men) bring down (what they desire) from you, as the waters (descend) from the top of the mountain; desirous of food, they approach you, who are accessible to praise, with these their eulogies, as (eagerly as) coursers rush to battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The same verse is addressed to Agni in S─Бmaveda

Jamison Brereton

Like waters forth from the back of a mountain, they proceeded forth from you along with solemn words and sacrifices, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

By my analysis this vs. matches 4 in structure and in referents, forming with 4 a ring around the omphalos vs. 5. In the first p─Бda the unspecified pair (ubh├бyoс╕е тАж ay├│с╕е тАЬof both of theseтАЭ) refers, in my view (as also, apparently, Geldner), to the two kr├бndas─л (lit. тАШwar-criesтАЩ, viz., opposing forces) of 4d; Indra has mastery over the manly power of both of them, as vs. 5 has already implied. The verb of 6b, h├бvante, doubles br├бvaite in 4d semantically; both refer to verbal appeals to Indra for help in battle. The two forces referred to in an oblique case in p─Бda a return as subject in p─Бda d, with yet another 3rd du. med. subjunctive, vitantasa├нte. Pace Geldner, who gives them different roles, the locc. in c are parallel and match those of 4c, expressing what is at stake in the battle. Although it might seem odd to name a vс╣Ыtr├б- as a stake, I think the point is that the battle may be about confronting an obstacle or about acquiring a rich dwelling place. KleinтАЩs tr. (DGRV II.159) тАЬwhen they battle each other in the (struggle with the) obstacle or in (the struggle for) great dwelling space rich in heroesтАЭ reflects the same view. See Schaeffer (Intens. 126-27) for detailed disc. A similar use of vс╣Ыtr├йс╣гu is found in the next hymn (VI.26.2), where it is implicitly parallel to g├│с╣гu, an expression for the stakes.

I take the subordinator y├бd─л in b as representing y├бd + ─л (тАШwhenтАЩ + acc. particle) (as described pp. 305-9 in my 2002 article тАЬRigvedic s─лm and ─лm), rather than conditional y├бdi тАШifтАЩ. All that needs to be done is to insert a notional word space between y├бd and ─л. The p─Бda could use an overt acc. (─л тАШhimтАЩ, as obj. of h├бvante), and тАШifтАЩ does not make sense.

The published translation implicitly reflects a similar analysis of y├бdi in d, but I now think that interpr. is probably incorrect. In favor of it is the parallelism with the matched vs. 4, which contains two parallel y├бd clauses. But several factors, both formal and functional, weigh against it: the final i of y├бdi is short and does not occur before a cons. cluster, which elsewhere facilitates the shortening of the particle ─л. Moreover, an acc. referent is not necessary to the clause, since the verb is a reciprocal middle (though see I.131.3, also with med. v├н тИЪtaс╣Гs, v├н tv─Б tatasre тАЬThey have tussled over you,тАЭ a passage that also contains a loc. of the stakes). The published translation also renders the subjunctive vitantasa├нte as an indicative. I now think that the conditional y├бdi and the subjunctive contribute to the same semantic effect. For a full revised tr. see below.

On the assumption that cd forms a single dependent clause (as it does in the published translation and in Geldner), the y├бdi is too deep in the clause, following not only the nom. du.

adj. vy├бcasvant─Б that opens p─Бda d but also the complex loc. phrase that occupies p─Бda c. This problem could be easily remedied by connecting c with b, rather than with d, leaving y├бdi in standard 2nd position in a clause now consisting only of d. The only obstacle to that reassignment is my interpr. of mah├бс╕е, which in the published translation I take as a sentential adverb and construe with vitantasa├нte (тАЬтАж keep tussling mightilyтАЭ). However, that interpr. is quite fragile, esp. because of the position of mah├бс╕е, and I am happy to abandon it, though I do not have a particularly good alternative suggestion. Schaeffer (Intens. 128) first suggests that it is an adverb, with adjectival aspirations (not her phrase), construed with the following phrase nс╣Ыv├бti kс╣г├бye, in the manner of OldenbergтАЩs (ZDMG 55 [1901]: 270-71) interpr. of mah├│ r─Бy├й тАЬm├дchtiglich zu ReichtumтАЭ ├а тАЬzu m├дchtigem ReichtumтАЭ – in this instance тАЬm├дchtiglich m├дnnerreiches LandтАЭ ├а тАЬgrosses m├дnnerreiches Land.тАЭ Alternatively she suggests it could be an acc. pl. with gapped dev─Б╠Бn as a goal or obj. of vitantasa├нte (тАЬsooft die zwei тАж (V├╢lkerschaften) die Grossen (G├╢tter) angehen тАжтАЭ). This second suggestion seems quite implausible, but the first one is possible, in the absence of anything better. In any event, it is essentially the interpr. given by Geldner (тАЬum einen grossen m├дnnerreichen WohnsitzтАЭ), however he arrived at it. (Judging from his n.

6cd it rests on S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs high-handed glossing of maho with loc. mahati.) KleinтАЩs tr. тАЬgreat dwelling space rich in heroesтАЭ (see above) simply follows Geldner and also shows a quasi-adj. interpr. of mah├бс╕е.

Putting all this together, I offer the revised translation: тАЬHe is master of the manly power of both of these (armies) when the ritual adepts call on him in the clash, whether an obstacle or a dwelling place rich in men is at issue тАФ if the two (armies) in their expansion will keep tussling mightily back and forth with one another.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the person n of that vast Indra, celebrated by praises and prayers, ever increase; Indra, whom neither years nor months make old, nor days enfeeble.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra, whom the autumns do not age, nor do the months, nor days make leanтАФ
may his body, even though he is fully grown, grow stronger while it is being celebrated by praises and solemn words.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As usual, ary├бс╕е has a number of possible interpr. Geldner takes it as nom. pl.

identical to the s┼лr├бyaс╕е in d. Oldenberg suggests either acc. pl. or abl. sg. without choosing one. Thieme (Fremdling, 73-74) opts for the abl. sg., which he construes (as does Oldenberg) with the splv. nс╣Ы╠Бtam─Бsaс╕е: тАЬтАж als unsere, im Vergleich zum Fremdling sehr heldenhaften Schutzherren тАжтАЭ But of course an ablative with a superlative would be highly unusual (though Oldenberg offers a single parallel and a ref. to Delbr├╝ckтАЩs Vgl.

Syn.). I also take it as an abl., but suggest construing it with pur├бс╕е. I now see that this is also problematic, since it is not clear that pur├бс╕е ever takes the abl. Grassmann gives two exx.: but in IV.7.9 the supposed abl. is a gen. and construed elsewhere; in III.53.23 the form in question (├б┼Ыv─Бn) could be either an abl. sg. or an acc. pl. in sandhi.

Nonetheless I hold to this interpr. Although pur├бс╕е + ABL is not a robust construction, the related pur─Б╠Бis regularly found with the abl. Here I would suggest that we have a sort of pun. The lexeme pur├бс╕е + тИЪdh─Б тАШset in front, installтАЩ is of course very common, and that phrase is found here, dadhir├й pur├│ naс╕е. Although, as I just said, to express тАЬahead of / in front of the strangerтАЭ we might expect ary├бс╕е [abl.] тАж pur─Б╠Б, there was interference with the VP dadhir├й pur├│ naс╕е тАЬthey have set us in front,тАЭ and pur├бс╕е prevailed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Each of these vss. contains at least one derivative of nс╣Ы╠Б- тАШ(superior) manтАЩ: 6a nс╣Ыmс╣З├бm, 6c nс╣Ыv├бti, 7c nс╣Ы╠Бtam─Бsaс╕е, 8d nс╣Ыс╣г├бhye.

Griffith

That Indra whom nor months nor autumn seasons wither with age, nor fleeting days enfeeble,-
Still may his body Wax, e’en now so mighty, glorified by the lauds and hymns that praise him.

Geldner

Zu Indra, den die Herbste nicht alt machen noch die Monate und Tage abmagern. Obwohl er schon ausgewachsen ist, soll sein Leib noch wachsen, wenn er mit Lobges├дngen und Preisreden gefeiert wird.

Grassmann

Den Jahre nicht, noch Monde altern machen, den nicht der Lauf der Tage abzehrt, Indra, Auch dem erwachsnen wachse doch sein Leib noch, wenn er durch Spruch gepriesen wird und Lieder.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorified by us, he bows not down to the robust, nor to the resolute, nor to the person vering (worshipper) who is instrumental gated by the (irreligious) Dasyus; the lofty mountains are easy of access o Indra; to him there is a bottom in the (lowest) deep.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He does not bow to the tough, nor to the stubborn, nor to the vaunting one sped by the Dasyus, when he receives praise.
Even the towering mountains are flatlands for Indra. Even in the deep there is a ford for him.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition ed. resolves the contraction across p─Бda boundary of yajatr├йndra as yajatr─Б╠Б├нndra. This must be a careless error, since the Pp. has yajatra ├нndra, and the stem y├бjatra- has root accent.

Each of these vss. contains at least one derivative of nс╣Ы╠Б- тАШ(superior) manтАЩ: 6a nс╣Ыmс╣З├бm, 6c nс╣Ыv├бti, 7c nс╣Ы╠Бtam─Бsaс╕е, 8d nс╣Ыс╣г├бhye.

Griffith

Extolled, he bends not to the strong, the steadfast, nor to the bold incited by the Dasyu.
High mountains are as level plains to Indra: even in the deep he finds firm ground to rest on.

Geldner

Er weicht nicht dem Z├дhen noch dem Festen, nicht dem ├Ьberm├дchtigen, von den Dasyu┬┤s Getriebenen, wenn er gepriesen wird. Auch die hohen Berge sind f├╝r Indra nur Ebenen, selbst im Tiefen findet er Grund.

Grassmann

Nicht beugt er sich dem Starren, noch dem Festen, der Donnrer nicht vor frechem D├дmondiener; Auch hohe Berge sind dem Indra eben, auch in der Tiefe findet festen Grund er.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPowerful Indra, drinker of the soma, (actuated) by a profound and comprehensive (purpose), grant us food and strength; be ever diligent, benevolent Indra, for our protection by day and by night.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With a (vessel) that is deep and wide, o bearer of the vessel, hold forth to us refreshments and prizes, you drinker of the pressings,
and stand erect with your help, allowing no harm, at the early
brightening of the night, at its final turn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c = I.177.5c and X.89.17c. Geldner (fld. by Klein, DGRV I.458) construes v├бstoс╕е with vidy─Б╠Бma (тАЬM├╢chten wir S├дnger тАж den neuen Tag erlebenтАЭ), but wellattested v├бstoс╕е is otherwise a temporal expression тАШat dawn, in the morningтАЩ. In both the other passages, the p─Бda in question is adjoined by a p─Бda that likewise begins vidy─Б╠Бma (following in I.177.5, preceding in X.89.17), and the obj. of that vidy─Б╠Бma can be assumed with the one in the repeated p─Бda. The d p─Бda of X.89.17 is almost identical to d here, with the substitution of a different poetic family: vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бmitr─Бс╕е for our bhar├бdv─Бj─Бс╕е.

The function and position of ut├б in d are unclear. The published translation implicitly assumes that it loosely connects the 2nd hemistich with the 1st (тАЬAnd with your help тАжтАЭ), but locating this clausal conjunction in 2nd position of the 2nd p─Бda of what itтАЩs conjoining would be an irrational poetic strategy. I now think it likely that it conjoins the temporal expressions v├бstoс╕е and n┼лn├бm, and I would alter the tr. to тАЬWith your help тАж might we Bharadv─Бjas know (this), as we sing at dawn and also nowтАЭ (or тАЬmight we know (this) at dawn and also now, as we singтАЭ). The curiosity then is the position of te, which can only belong to something in the preceding p─Бda: either тАЬwith your helpтАЭ (as I take it in the published translation) or тАЬas we sing to you.тАЭ I suppose that ut├бтАЩs strong tendency to take 1st position makes it a natural host for enclitics even when it is not so located, but it really seems odd that it would sweep te up and away from the elements it should be limiting.

Griffith

Impetuous Speeder through all depth and distance, give strengthening food, thou drinker of the juices.
Stand up erect to help us, unreluctant, what time the gloom of night brightens to morning.

Geldner

In einem tiefen weiten Humpen, du Humpenhalter, reiche uns Speisegen├╝sse, Belohnungen, du Somatrinker. Steh fein aufrecht mit deiner Hilfe, vor Schaden bewahrend, im Hellwerden des Dunkels in der Entscheidungsstunde!

Grassmann

In tiefem, weitem Krug, o krugbegabter, reich Tr├дnk’ und Speisen uns, o Somatrinker, Steh aufrecht bald, mit deiner Huld nicht s├дumend, wenn erstes Licht sich zeigt im Morgendunkel.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдирд╛рдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддреАрдирд╛рдВ рдЪ рдиреЗрддрд╛рд░рдореН рдЕрднреАрдХреЗ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рд╕рдЪрд╕реНрд╡ рд╕реЗрд╡рд╕реНрдп ред рдЗрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рд╕рдВрдирд┐рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдЪреНрдЪ рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рдЕрдореБрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд░реЛрд╢реНрдЪ ред рд╡рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджреЛрд╜рдиреБрдХреНрддреЗрди рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреЗрди рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердГ ред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдВ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ рд░рдХреНрд╖ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЕрдорд╛ рдЪ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рдЪ ред рдЕрдореЗрддрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣рдирд╛рдо ред рдЕрд░рдгреНрдпреЗ рдХрд╛рдирдиреЗ рдЪ рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ рддрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖ ред рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╢рддрд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдГ рд╢рддрд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛рдиреН рдорджреЗрдо рд╣реГрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдо рее рее резрео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAccompany, Indra, the leader in battle for his protection; defend him against a near (or distant) foe; protect him from an enemy, whether in (his) house or in a forest, and may we, blessed with excellent male descendants, be happy for a hundred winters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Accompany our leader to help him at the close encounter, or protect him from harm from here, Indra.
Protect him from harm at home and in the wilderness. тАУ Having good heroes might we rejoice for a hundred winters.

Griffith

Hasting to help, come hither and protect him, keep him from harm when he is here, O Indra.
At home, abroad, from injury preserve him. May brave sons gladden us through a hundred winters.

Geldner

Sei mit dem Anf├╝hrer zu seinem Schutz in der Entscheidung, oder beh├╝te ihn von hier aus vor Schaden, Indra! Beh├╝te ihn daheim und in der Wildnis vor Schaden! Wir wollen hundert Winter lebend als Meister frohlocken.

Grassmann

Dem F├╝hrer hilf zu Kr├дftigung im Kampfe, besch├╝tze hier, o Indra, ihn vor Schaden; Sch├╝tz ihn daheim vor Leid und in der Ferne; froh sei’n wir, reich an S├╢hnen, hundert Winter.

Elizarenkova

  • рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░:
  • рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬреЛ рдмрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреНрдпрдГ

  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН ! рдЖрдк (рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЕрднреАрдХреЗ) рд╕рдореАрдк рдореЗрдВ (рдирд╛рдпрдореН) рдиреНрдпрд╛рдп рдХреЛ (рд╕рдЪрд╕реНрд╡) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реВрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ (рдЗрддрдГ) рдпрд╣рд╛рдБ рд╕реЗ (рд╡рд╛) рд╡рд╛ (рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реЗ (рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ рдФрд░ (рдПрдирдореН) рдЗрд╕рдХреА (рдЕрдорд╛) рдЧреГрд╣ рдореЗрдВ рдФрд░ (рдЕрд░рдгреНрдпреЗ) рд╡рди рдореЗрдВ (рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ (рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ, рдЪ) рдФрд░ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рд╕реЗ рднреА, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рд╡реАрд░ рдЬрд┐рдирдХреЗ рдРрд╕реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╢рддрд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдГ) рд╕реМ рд╡рд░реНрд╖ рдкрд░реНрдпрдиреНрдд (рдорджреЗрдо) рдЖрдирдиреНрдж рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрди рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рджреВрд░ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдореАрдк рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╣реБрдП рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдЪрд░рдг рдФрд░ рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕ рд╕реЗ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЛ рдмреЭрд╛рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдмрд╕реНрддреА рдФрд░ рдЬрдЩреНрдЧрд▓реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерезрежрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛, рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЪреМрдмреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЕрдард╛рд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рддреНрд╡рдорд╡рд╕реЗрд╜рднреАрдХреЗ рдирд╛рдпрдВ рд╕рдЪрд╕реНрд╡, рдЗрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ рдкрд╛рд╣реНрдпреЗрдирдордорд╛рд╜рд░рдгреНрдпреЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ рд░рд┐рд╖рд╢реНрдЪ рдпрддрдГ рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╢рддрд╣рд┐рдорд╛ рдорджреЗрдо реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдЪрд╕реНрд╡) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рдирд╛рдпрдореН) рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдореН (рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдп (рдЕрднреАрдХреЗ) рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ (рдЗрддрдГ) (рд╡рд╛) (рддрдореН) (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН рд╡рд╛ (рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐) (рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХрд╛рддреН (рдЕрдорд╛) рдЧреГрд╣реЗ (рдЪ) (рдПрдирдореН) (рдЕрд░рдгреНрдпреЗ) (рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐) (рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рддреН (рдорджреЗрдо) рдЖрдирдиреНрджреЗрдо (рд╢рддрд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдГ) рд╢рддрдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдгрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛ рд╡реАрд░рд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рджреВрд░реЗ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдЪрд░рдгрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрд┐рддрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рд╡рд╕рддрд┐рд╖реБ рдЬрдЩреНрдЧрд▓реЗрд╖реБ рдЪ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ реерезрежрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреА рджреВрд░ рд╡ рдЬрд╡рд│ рдЕрд╕рд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреА рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдЪрд░рдг рд╡ рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕ рдпрд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЗ рдмреБрджреНрдзреА рд╡рд╛рдврд╡реВрди рд╢рд╣рд░рд╛рдд рд╡ рдЬрдВрдЧрд▓рд╛рдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резреж рее
